<Author>MaxGS
<Content>Great hotel at the center of Paris We stayed at the Splendid Etoile for 5 nights in October 2008. We chose the hotel for its location and on the basis of favourable traveller reviews. It turned out to be a great choice! The hotel is small, quiet, yet centrally located on one of the avenues radiating from the Arc of Triumph. The metro/RER station (Charles de Gaulle Etoile) is right outside the main entrance of the hotel. From this station you can get directly on the RER going to Eurodisney; the jounrey takes about 35 to 40 minutes. The Air France bus service from Charles de Gaulle airport runs from just across the street. There is also a taxi rank just a few meters up the road. The hotel offers a buffet breakfast for 23 euro per person (which is somewhat expensive) but does have a good selection of croissants, baguettes, cake, cheese, ham, cereal, scrambled / boiled eggs, fruit, tea, coffee and hot chocolate. The hotel also has a restaurant open for lunch/dinner and there is a great variety of cafes and restaurants in the neighbourhood. Our room was spacious, the beds were comfortable, the bathroom was clean. The gentlemen at the reception were very friendly, polite and eager to help, give directions, call a taxi etc. Overall, we had a very pleasant stay at the Splendid Etoile and would definitely stay there again!  
<Date>Nov 14, 2008

<Author>sandknitz
<Content>Splendid indeed! I recently spent four nights at Splendid Etoile and am so grateful I did! Since this was my first trip to Paris and I was a woman traveling alone, I did a lot of research and read many reviews prior to booking my hotel. Splendid Etoile far exceeded my expectations!While it may seem a bit pricey, it was worth every penny! First, its location is incredibly convenient . . . the Air France bus from CDG drops off right across the street and the RER/Metro station is a few steps from the front door. In addition, I was easily able to walk to the Arc, the Champs-Elysees, the Bateaux-Mouches on the Seine and the Eiffel Tour. You can also catch the les Cars Rouge minutes away on the Champs-Elysees near the Arc.I was very fortunate to get a corner room, so I had a magnificent postcard-like view of the Arc de Triomphe through my floor to ceiling windows which I left open during my waking hours while in the room. Day and night, it was mesmerizing.I appreciated the intimate lobby. My room was lovely and spotless. The staff was very attentive and the concierges were all so helpful!The perfect ending to my magical trip happened my last afternoon there. After returning to my room and throwing open my windows to breathe in a little more of Paris, I was treated to a sun shower immediately followed by a huge double rainbow out my window over the Arc.This was a life long dream fulfilled, and the Splendid Etoile truly enhanced the entire experience. I look forward to the day when I am able to return with my husband!

<Author>Smood
<Content>Paris gem Had a wonderful two night stay here at end of September. Air France Bus from Charles de Gaulle (Line 2) stops just over the road from the Hotel. Entrance to Etoile Metro station is also just over the road. We arrived at about 11am and thought we'd chance it to see if our room was ready. Check-in staff and Concierge were fantastic - they estimated that room would be ready in 10 minutes and were delighted when we were given the all clear after 3! Stayed in Room 306 - great size, with two balconies opening out onto the street with a wonderful view of the Arc de Triomphe to the side . Had requested the view when booking but you never know until you get there. Room 307 might have had a direct view of the Arc from within the room but we were delighted with the size and comfort of 306. Concierge also recommended L'Empereur cafe, immediately over the road from the hotel entrance and we ate there a couple of times - a good selection of prix fix menus, especially the breakfast and brunch. We never ate in the hotel so couldn't comment on that aspect. We tried Le Cristal cafe once, behind the hotel on the next Avenue over leading from the Arc. Ordered here from the prix fix and ate what they bought to the table, only to find that we were being charged for each item that we ate - tourists beware! Overall a wonderful experience with great access to/from the airport and to the metro system. Couldn't fault the hotel.

<Author>megmarc
<Content>Awesome first experience in Paris Let me start by saying that this was my wife and I's first trip to Paris, so I have no perspective on what other hotels are like and my compete basis of comparison for making this reservation was TripAdvisor.The location is awesome, because it is on the Champs Elysees, but also because it is right across from a Metro, which we learned will take you anywhere. The areas around the hotel were great for finding great shopping, cafes and an afternoon bottle of wine.We stayed a week in late September in room 309, a Jr. Suite located on the 4th floor. We did not have a view of the Arch but knew that and preferred the Jr. Suite. I must admit that our first impression of the Jr. Suite was disappointing as it did not look as grand as the picture on the web site, but we soon got used to it and were very very happy with our choice. It was a bit expensive, but I'm guessing that is just Paris.The bathrooms appear to be reasonably new and are very well appointed. I was pleasantly surprised just how well done they were. We asked that the twin beds be converted to a king which they took care of for us. The appointments are minimal but very efficient. We had two very grand windows, one in each room, that opened up onto the street. Our view, while not of the ADT, was of a normal Paris street, and we found it very nice. The adjacent room was small but also very efficent and included a TV, mini bar and small table. All better than we expected.The in room internet sucked but they have a free internet station downstairs that was almost always available and it worked great.We did not request the breakfast package and did not use the bar, so I dont have any thoughts on those.The strength of the Hotel Splendid is the staff. They are remarkable. Some of the nicest people I have ever encountered in a hotel. We have traveled extensively and I would match them up against anyplace we have stayed. The front desk staff made you feel at home every time you entered the hotel. They helped us with everything from how to ask for something in French to how to request a refund of the VAT tax on purchased items. They were always friendly and helpfull. I would recommend this place to anyone.

<Author>CDCS
<Content>Highly recommended hotel Stayed in this hotel for 2 nights in September. I have stayed in a number of different hotel in Paris and this is by far and away the best. The location is fantastic - views of the Arc de Triomphe as other reviewers have mentioned. And the Air Fance bus from the airports will leave you practically at the door of the hotel. <Author>solent_blue_ling
<Content>A perfect Paris hotel We stayed at The Splendid Etoile for 3 nights Bed and Breakfast in August and I am delighted to say that it met all my expectations. This hotel is a pricey 4 star but certainly ticks all your boxes for a luxury romantic Parisienne break. After shopping round for the best rate I found a deal on eurostars own website which gave you the 3rd night free and breakfast and a pound upgrade to 1st class seats on the train. I then contacted the hotel direct to request an upgrade to a superior room before we arrived, as I wanted to ensure that we had a room with a view. Our room was the corner room on the 4th floor and the view was just magical. We had most amazing view of the Arc de Triomphe from the 2 balconies in the bedroom, and my husband boasted that he could even see the top of the Eiffel Tower from the balcony in the bathroom! I couldnt fault the standard of the furnishings in the room which was spotlessly maintained. The Buffet Breakfast was 2 die for and there was so much food on offer that it kept us going until tea time (.... a huge benefit in Paris as the restaurants are ridiculously over priced ! ) One word of warning though, is that breakfast is only served until 10.30am prompt - not until 12pm or 11.30am as the staff and hotel literature advise you ! We witnessed a number of dissapointed hungry guests being turned away at 10.31am. The hotel was superbly located at the top of the Champs Elysee which caters for those of you who either want to walk or take the metro. Sadly the hotel bar was closed throughout our stay which left us feeling a little short changed on the facilities front - but the staff were professional, polite and discreet at all times and I would definately return again.

<Content>Perfection! For our first ever trip to Paris, my husband and I booked a superior room, requesting a direct view of the Arc, at the Hotel Splendid Etoile. After much fretting over whether or not the hotel and room would live up to the reviews, that I poured over on this site, I can report that our 9-day stay (7-21 to 7-29-08) at this property was absolute perfection. We checked in to Room #507, which had a wrap around balcony accessible from both the bathroom and the bedroom, and the most beautiful and direct view of the Arc de Triomphe that anyone could hope for. As a bonus, because we were 5 floors up, we also had a view of the Eiffel Tower. The view literally took my breath away, as I had not expected such a treat.We had a large closet with multiple shelves and full length mirrors, a safe, mini-refrigerator, both a desk  table with chairs and a large double bed with a great mattress. The bathroom was huge, with the best water pressure of any shower I have ever experienced in a hotel. Our room was spacious, clean and I didn't want to leave!Right outside the front door was the Metro, a taxi stand, the Air France bus stop, and access to the RER.Everyone of staff that we came in contact with, were attentive, friendly and welcoming. I would not hesitate to book this hotel again.

<Author>BrazAustralia
<Content>terrific place, great location We have just returned to Australia after a 4 night stay at the Splendid, and Splendid it was too....echoing all of the favourable comments on this site, I would add that I was more than pleasantly suprised by the size and style of the room, and can confirm again that Farouk is extremely good at his job- by the way, he used to be a fast bowler in Pakistan, and was considering going to Australia for coaching by Lillee and Thommo- he chose Paris and the hospitality industry- good new for all of us I'd say....Anyway, back to the hotel. We stayed in a superior room, room 403- with the exceptional view of the Arc from the balcony- probably fairer to call it a balcony rather than a terrace by the way, wouldn't really be able to hold a cocktail party out there! The room was MUCH bigger than I had expected, should even impress Americans. It had an entrance hall, bathroom off it, and a door to the bedroom that could be shut, so there is an extra level of privacy from the bathroom to the bedroom if you get my drift. Good size wardrobe, good flat screen TV, but dodgy air conditioning- we couldn't get it to move from freezing or off, but to be honest we are low maintenace guests, we reported it once and then didn't worry about it again. Fussy people would probably be whingeing round about now I expect.Tiny lift up- as per usual in Paris- charming lobby, bar area, and a little ( unairconditioned) phone box size room with an internet connected PC ( free to use) for all those people who aren't bringing laptops on holidays with them, but still need to check emails etc. As per this sites advise, we didn't eat at the hotel- Farouk in fact pointed out a great breakfast cafe down the road a bit , where he goes- much better than the place over the road.It really is ridiculously handy for transport- RER station right outside the door, Cab rank 10 metres away, metro stop 200 metres, and the 14 euro Air France bus to CDG airport just over the road- brilliantly located. We strolled under the Arc to the Champs Elysee for people watching, and visited quite a few of the local bars/ bistros where the Euro's were on TV every night.Anyway, I would stay there again like a shot- that's how good it is- well priced for what you get, and fully worth its high rating on this site- au revoir Hotel Splendid Etoile!

<Author>eklektra
<Content>Fantastic Gem of A Hotel The Hotel is in a fantastic, quiet neighborhood just one block from the Arc de Triomphe and Champs Elysees and is surrounded by many fabulous cafes and restaurants. The front desk staff is fantastic and attentive even when the lobby is crowded with people. Farooq is a national treasure and went above and beyond with assisting us. The Air France bus stops directing across the street which provided easy, hassle free transportation to CDG/Roissy. They dropped at our terminal. There is a cab stand and a metro stop steps from the hotel... actual steps not a 15 minute walk steps. A walk to the Eiffel Tower took about 20 minutes. The Louvre and other places of interest for us took about 45, but Paris is a city for walking. All rooms do not have a view of the Arc. Sadly ours did not, but it was spacious and comfortable just the same. If I recall 207, a superior room, had the postcard view from the terrace. I would definitely return!

<Author>Unver
<Content>A Nice weekend in Pairs The hotel is located in the very center of the city just across the famous Arc de Triumph. Acess to the hotel from the CDG airport with the buses of Air France is very easy. They stop just at the corner of the street. The buses are comfortable and cheap relatively to taxis. The room I stayed was a superior one with a balcony and a view of Arc de Triumph. The room was quite large for a couple even with a child. The only bad experience we had was about the hair dryer in our room. It was not operating and when we asked for a new one they said that they can not get a working one and they did not.Altough the room was clean and well decorated it requires a renovation in coming one or two years. The concierge was helpfull and depending on whom sits on the front desk you could get english speaking stuff (This is something extraordinary in France)Overall, it is not cheap hotel but if you want to be in the city center and have ease of access to both metro and buses it is good choice.

<Author>jpclark9
<Content>Great location, Great hotel Nice hotel, central enough for walking to many must see sights. The balcony and view of the arc make for some memorable photos. We had to wait to get into our room, but the front desk ordered us complimentary coffee and chocolate for the short wait. The rooms are a good size for European standards, but a little cramped with a roll away for a third person. We loved the ease of the shuttle bus stop across the street from the hotel when arriving from the airport; however, if taking a train out of Paris, be sure to pre-order your taxi in plenty of time for an a.m. pickup in front of the hotel. It takes a little time to get to the train stations in morning traffic and we nearly missed our train to the alps due to the fact that it took 30 minutes to get a taxi. Overall a very nice stay. Next visit I think I will split my time between this hotel and another closer to the Latin Quarter.

<Author>Zippyzazoo
<Content>Splendidly too quiet for me, though nice for the right person. I stayed here a few months ago. It was my first time traveling based on reviews from Tripadvisor.comWell, I learned that I am not looking for the same things as most travelers. Everyone seems concerned with how posh and quiet it is. I am only 34 and when I go out of town, I want to experience the city. The hotel plays a large part in that experience as I am always going too and from it.The neighborhood is nice, but a sleepy bedroom community, for Paris that is. While sightseeing you have to pass all the fun communities with plentiful cafes and parks to come back to the Splendid. I would have preferred a hotel in the 6th, 5th near the Pantheon or Ile de la Cite, after visiting them. There you have more cafes with the chairs on the sidewalks in rows, and art galleries and tons of unique boutiques, bakeries and more. That being said, it may be the perfect hotel for those who want peace and quiet ( though there is a bar down the sidestreet, that you can hear drunks yelling sometimes. I ran to my balcony to watch, excited by the prospect of life, they were too far to see though.) The streets had few people and no street life. Granted, it was August.The Champs is very close, but mostly just a bunch of shops I have here. Walk through it on your way to somewhere.The Arc de Triomphe is close, but once you have seen it...The hotel was nice. I paid a little more than I wanted to because of the reviews on here. I would have gladly paid more for a more idealized Parisian neighborhood and atmosphere. Like on TV, and that is what you get in the other neighborhoods I mentioned.I had some form of junior suite. Walk through the door,then a little cloakroom or place to put luggage and hang coats with a door that shut it from the bedroom, then the bedroom, pretty windows that sealed off traffic noise, a balcony, then to the right of the bedroom is a little sitting room, and off of that the bathroom, which was very nice and large for Europe. Semi-mildewy shower curtain. The room had a balcony and a view of a pretty Cap-Gemini Consulting office building. Nothing at all to look at to the left or the right.Breakfast was good! I liked it. Not too different from other hotels I have stayed at in London. Bins with eggs, bacon and sausage in one small area, and a longer table with breads, meats, cheeses, fruit, cereal and beverages. The entire breakfast room is smaller than most master bedrooms in the U.S. I look forward to breakfast as I like to see the other travelers and get my bearings for the day.There is not a bar that I noticed and no place where other patrons congregate or one can talk to the staff in a less formal manner.Overall, a nice place, but not worth the #8 spot on here in my opinion. Not even close. Tripadvisor needs to come up with a better ratings system besides singles, families and romance.

Please do youself a favor and refrain from booking this hotel. We made the mistake and would hate to see other people from making the same mistake. <Author>travelingprince
<Content>Romantic and delightful Hotel Got back 10-25 -07 from Paris, and 4 nights at the Hotel Splendid- would have liked to stay longer but the World Cup rugby finals took all the rooms months earlier. The only negative(get this out of the way)-- The room is average by Paris standards- a little small to me- first trip to Euroupe. The room is beautifully appointed, lovely furniture, chandeliers, flat screen tv, decent closet space. The view is great- The hotel is next to the Arc de Triumph- ask for a view room- its worth it. Very quiet inside(double pane windows)-- Three sets of balconies. Spotless, -little touches- like the great key , towel warmer, bidet??, robes, extra thick towels. The tub is deep and long enough but if you're hips are over 40 you might get stuck. Great location-- Up the Champs Elyssis- the metro literally 10 steps from your hotel- 5-7 minutes to most of the sights. A great cafe across the street- 9-13 euro's for a great breakfast. Hotel charges 22euros( I didn''t think it was worth the difference-- they're was much more food than I could eat. ) The service is 5*- Farooq the head conciege is dedicated to making everything go smoothly- storing our luggage when we planned to go away- calling cabs( even when they're impossible to get), helping with any excusion or transportation plan you can think of. Free internet which came in handy while we watched the fires burn near our San Diego home- and kept on track with our 3rd aniversary vacation. There's even a shuttle that leaves all day and night to the airport for 25Euros for 2. Farooq personally helped drag all five peices across the street to the shuttle. The stuck-up rude to Americans French were not anywhere near this place. It was worth it to me to pay a few more Euros to have a beautiful setting,convienyent location, and great service. And yes- Our home it ca-va-(o.k.)

<Author>deputysher
<Content>WOW what a fantastic property, fantastic location, and caring staff! I chose this hotel due to previous reviews on TripAdvisor and we were not disappointed. While comparing the rates, we decided to splurge for a suite and we were not disappointed. We had the corner suite which overlooked not only the Arc but also Rue de Carnot. The rooms were spacious and the bathroom beautifully appointed. We loved it.The view from our room was fabulous -- we could see not only the Arc but also the Eiffel Tower -- you just can't get any better than that! We felt so charmed and special and delighted by this! We loved having the suite because with jet lag, sometimes one of us was up in the living room reading or watching TV, while the other was in the bedroom sleeping. There were pocket door separating the two so it was very handy.Other reviews mention the busy traffic and quietness of the rooms. We were astounded by the fact that the thick curtains, which are drawn at night over closed windows, TOTALLY blocked out the sounds of traffic, sirens, and helicopters. Yes, helicopters! The first morning we were there, there was some type of traffic accident or medical emergency on the round about around the Arc. Many, many emergency vehicles came including a helicopter, presumably to remove the injured. Traffic came to a dead standstill, and probably caused havoc throughout this part of Paris.We walked to the Eiffel Tower at night (the concierge said it was about 15 minutes but that must be in 'french walk speed' as it took us about 30 minutes. We thoroughly enjoyed the walk and especially loved seeing the tower lit up. We took a cab back and it was only 6 euro, well worth it as our feet were tired by then.We also got brave and took the Metro (subway) to the Louvre, based on Farooq's advice. The entrance to the Metro is right next to the hotel - it can't get any easier! We also took the Air France bus from DeGualle Airport based on Farooq's advice and were happy we did. It was only $13euro each and let us off directly across from the hotel. That was amazing!The evening concierges recommended two restaurants that were very good. One was a brasserie just 2 blocks away, and the other was a small restaurant about 3 blocks away. Both were excellent though the bill at the restaurant was scary -- $188 euro, but we chalked that up to being in Paris!I would definitely stay at this hotel each and every future visit to Paris. We previously stayed in St. Germaine des Pres, but the service here was outstanding and really made the difference for us.

<Author>PingleNJ
<Content>Spectacular Visit (-- in spite of a train strike) We stayed at the Splendid Etoile for 3 nights. The location is fantastic, with a great view of the Arc from the room balcony. The rooms were very nice and very clean. Although the hotel is in a bustling area, it was completely quiet at night with little to no street noise, making for a very comfortable stay. While the accommodations were excellent, the best reason to stay at the Splendid Etoile was the staff. Each and every staff member was professional, kind and considerate, personal, polite and incredibly accomodating. The day of our departure was quite untimely, in that a train strike went into effect the night before and we woke that morning with no train back to Geneva. Additionally, because of the strike, there were no available flights out, no available rental cars and the hotel was booked. Needless to say, it was a bit nerve racking -- but the concierge, Farooq, was incredibly comforting, continually reassuring us not to worry and that we would be taken care of. After numerous calls, he found us safe passage home. He went above and beyond to ensure that our wonderful Paris stay did not end in distress. We are incredibly grateful to the staff at the Splendid Etoile and especially to Farooq for his genuine kindness and caring. This is a great Paris hotel and as such, you need to book early!

<Author>DaniellepwALES
<Content>Great Location But Few Minor Issues I booked hotel based purely on T.A. reviews and must say the location cannot be faulted. However, I am surprised that the reviews did not mention the b/fast area. The hotel has approx. 57 rooms but only 8 tables in the b/fast area!! We waited for15 min. one morning for a table and thereafter went down REALLY early to get a table without having to wait. The staff in the hotel are friendly but I must say that the lady who runs the b/fast room made our stay very unpleasant. she run it like it was a military and it was very regimental-it would not have hurt her to smile once in a while. Two tips - I agree with a recent review that complained about 'rip off' taxi fares. We approached taxi driver directly outside hotel to ask how much it would be to take 4 of us to CDG, he quoted 30-35 Euros. When I asked Concerige, he said it would be 70 Euros, so you can guess who we chose!! So advice is, you are better off arranging your own taxi.Secondly, we decided to take the Air France shuttle to hotel on arrival ,again based purely on T.A. reviews.The only problem with that is that if you arrive in Terminal 3 as we did, you have to lug all of your luggage to Terminal 2 to catch shuttle. You have a long walk then catch the CDGVal to get shuttle. The journey from the airport to hotel, which stops right outside door, took one and a half hours, hence the reason for taking the taxi back to CDG. This might not bother some people but it's worth mentioning.The lift only carries 3 people which again is a problem if there are more of you in your party and during our 5 day stay, the bar was not open at all.All in all, our stay was a pleasant one and I would probably stay there again if only for the location but I was slightly disappointed that it didn't entirely live up to all the hype which is a shame.Also, I did not meet the celebrity that is Farouk as maybe it could have turned my stay around!

<Author>MadameKUnitedStates
<Content>I'm sad to say that I will never stay here again! Let me start by saying that this was my THIRD stay at this hotel (I loved it the first two times) and that I booked my stay directly with the hotel rather than one of the discount sites. You should also know that I speak fluent French so there was never a misunderstanding due to a language barrier. First of all, the beds are hard as rocks and instead of bed pillows, they only have shams on the beds - a big change from my last stay. The concierges' recommendations for restaurants were in most cases not worthwhile choices. More importantly, beware of the practice of some of the concierges to make arrangements with the hotel car driver to rip you off for local cab rides. We had agreed on a 30 Euro price one night ,(there were 5 of us) but were charged 50 Euros when we got back to the hotel! Farouq (the head concierge) met with me, apologized, and said that he knows the concierges should not try to rip off tthe customers by conspiring with the car drivers to pad the bill so they can make extra money, but beyond his apology, nothing else happened. After that, I called for our own cabs. When we checked out, we were charged for internet service in our rooms (when we had no computers with us!!) and over 35 Euros for long-distance phone calls which we did not make (as we used only our cell phones to make satellite calls). They took off the computer charge, but not the phone calls. When I returned home, I e-mailed and wrote the General Manager of the hotel (in French) and asked for a refund. I never even received a response, let alone a refund. The view and location are wonderful, but for the price of this hotel, I will stay somewhere else next time ---the Splendid no longer lives up to its name!!!  
<Date>Aug 12, 2007

<Author>MartinAB
<Content>Nice Hotel in a Terrific Location My wife and I just stayed at the Splendid Etoile for eight nights in a superior room. Overall, we would highly recommend this hotel. First, it is in a very convenient location for traveling from the airport and getting around the city. The Air France bus shuttle from the airport stops right across the street and the Metro entrance is also within a block. We often took the Metro to our destination (Louve, D鈥橭rsay, Latin Quarter etc.) and enjoyed the walk back to the Splendid Etoile taking different routes each day. Our room, number 503, had a nice view of the Arc and a pleasant balcony to enjoy the signs and sound of Paris. The room was a reasonable size and clean. The housekeeping staff is very good and on numerous occasions returned while we were out for dinner to tidy up the room. The concierge staff was fluent in English and provided friendly and helpful guidance. There is a nice convenience store just a block away which was great for morning fruit and yogurt. Unfortunately for us the bakery located at the end of Carnot Ave was open for only one day and then closed for vacation for the balance of our stay. It is a superb option for breakfast coffee, bread and pastries. We tried several of the restaurants within a short distance from the hotel and found L鈥橝rc, Lateral and Grande Armee to be decent. However, because you are so close to the Arc and Champs Elysee the local restaurant tend to be a little bit touristy. We would certainly return to the Splendid Etoile should our travels take us back to Paris.

<Content>Excellent service but beware of 1st floor The website through which I booked the hotel could only give me standard room so I had to try my luck when I arrived to see if there was a superior room. On the first stay (I had to check out the next day for meetings outside of Paris, and then checked in again 2 days later) I got a superior room. Everything was ok but I cannot say the room was new. I was told they would try, if no superior room they would give me a junior suite at the same price. I gladly said thank you thinking about the photo I saw from the candid travelers' photos...only to be disappointed later.When I returned (late in the evening), the only room available was junior suite on the first floor...I went in gladly, only to find out it's a standard room (with no TV), attached with a small room that looked nowhere like the candid traveler's photo of junior suite, that had no door in between, that had a make-shift kind of sofa bed with the TV and the bathroom. Wait...the most terrible thing I found was...there was no aircon but a big monster cooling machine about the size of a mid-sized fridge, which ridiculously split hot air out from the back of the machine back to inside the room!!! I could not open the window as it's on first floor hence too noisy. Apparently they told me all the rooms on 1st floor were all equipped with such monster only. I asked to change to a standard room but they said they did not have other room anymore. So they left a note for the front desk to arrange another room the next day if available.I was so upset...fortunately when I returned the next evening they gave me the magic room X07!!! That solved all the problems.I must say all the staff had very good attitude. The only problem I had was when I asked for a 10% hotel discount card for Lafayett the staff that had all the cards had disappeared for a coffee!!!. After waiting and the hotel paging without any sight of him, I had to leave for the shopping without that card (so I could not get discount on skincare items which were not on sale at that time)...The excellent location made up for the unpleasant experience. However, I will probably not stay here again. For that price I would try somewhere else next time.

<Content>Wonderful Experience My wife and I just returned from our first trip to Paris and everything was perfect, starting with this wonderful hotel. The staff and the room, we had seven days in one of the apartments and it was better than we had anticipated. Bathrooms were big, sitting room had spectacular views, and service was impeccable. We already have good friends booking rooms here for their first trip in September. We took the advice of others and ate breakfast on the street and that was great advice. Directly north of the hotel, opposite direction of the Arch and at the end of the street, is a wonderful pastry shop and a must. The district for the hotel is very French and we found the locals to be very friendly and courteous. Also, various wine vendors at the end of the street and great wine for the room can be purchased at very low prices; however, wine is about the only thing that is inexpensive, but it is worth it. We experienced none of the parisian attitude stories that had been told to us by others. Also, take the Air France bus from the airport as it stops directly at the base of the hotel. We took a taxi, lost the address and spent an hour looking like lost tourists: bus is a better option. Can鈥檛 wait to go back.

<Author>Andrew_M_7
<Content>An impressive hotel, highly recommended After reading the reviews, booked a three night stay. I had high expectations and the hotel did not disappoint. The legend that is the head of concierge, Farooq, was very helpful as were the rest of the staff. To give an example I had booked a trip on-line a few days before heading out to Paris and was having problems getting the voucher sent through to my hotmail. On arriving in Paris, which was the day of the dinner cruise that I had booked, I had still not recieved the necessary voucher. Farooq contacted the agency on my behalf, phoning the cell number left on their voice-mail and demandedthat they e-mail my voucher to the hotel which was with me 15 minuteslater, I only wished I had booked the trip through the hotel in the first place.The hotel is allegedly three star, but this can only be because they do not have a fantastic marble reception area!?(still perfectly clean and presentable), as everything else was first class. I had booked a relatively cheap deal through Expedia and was a little concerned that our room may be quite small, despite this we were upgraded to a superior room becuase the hotel was not quite full. The room was modern and large, spotlessly clean with a double balconyand view over the Arc.The hotel itself is in an excellent location with the Arc/Champs Elysees literally a stones throw away. It is also very convenient for the Metro (3 lines) and RER (1 line) - Charles de Gualle Etoile exit 5 - so you can get back from places like the Eiffel Tower/Moulin Rouge late at night (tip, although not advertised there is a late train on line 2 after the Moulin Rouge has finished so you can stay until the end). If you are doing a bit of travelling on the Metro/RER, I would recommend that you get a carnet (10) of tickets, as this saves you a bit of time and money.The breakfast was pretty good, however there are cafes nearby and a mini supermaket a little further down Avenue carnot where you can pick up water and snacks.All in all I would highly recommend the hotel for your stay.

<Author>Adam from Virginia
<Content>Great Hotel in a Convenient Location We stayed at this hotel from May 2 - 8, 2007. We enjoyed our stay very much. We booked a superior room through Travelocity (with an airfare package) for about 175 Euros (225 dollars) per night. For a 5th floor balcony room (503) with a full view of the Arc de Triomphe in Paris right next to a Metro stop and an Air France express bus, it is a steal! Our room was OK size for Europe, with two twin beds pushed together. (Hard foam mattresses that we liked, although the linens were very cheap feeling/scratchy -- definitely not the Westin Heavenly Bed!) Very nice marble bathroom with a tub/shower with very powerful water pressure. To get a good feel for the superior rooms in comparison to the regular rooms, go to the hotel's website -- they show them both. A great thing about this hotel is that the front desk staff and the concierge speak English. Before we left for Paris, we heard that everyone speaks English. We can tell you that this is nonsense. Everybody speaks English there like everybody speaks French in the United States. So having hotel staff that can get you pointed in the right direction when you arrive was very helpful. So the rooms are nice; the front desk staff are great; the lobby is cute (although smoking is allowed there); the maid service was exceptional; and it has an in-house restaurant for breakfast and dinner (it seemed vacant most of the time). We cannot comment on the food because we didn't eat there. However, we can tell you that the breakfast is 22 Euros (which based on the current exchange rate is about 29 dollars). Who needs a $29 breakfast? We ate the best baguettes/coissants we have ever had and a cup of coffee for breakfast like the locals for about 2 Euros. This leads us to tell you about the hotel's location. It is about perfect. It is surrounded by a hundred nearby restaurants of every type and plenty of convenience stores for snacks, beverages, toiletries, etc. Also, we found the French people to be courteous, friendly, helpful -- simply wonderful. Everywhere we went there were proud Parisians anxious to share their beautiful city. We felt honored to be among them all. One sidebar on the hotel reservation process to tell you about: We paid for a superior room and confirmed a high floor with a view of the Arc de Triomphe by email and by telephone. But when we arrived, they assigned us to a 1st floor room with a view of nothing. If you pay for the superior room upgrade, stand your ground like we did and we think you will find the staff willing to accomodate you appropriately -- they accomodated our request with little fuss. All in all, it is a very nice little city hotel in a great, safe, residential and commercial neighborhood near one of the city's greatest monuments. We highly recommend it and would stay there again (although maybe not at the current Superior room rack rate of 300 Euros!)  
<Date>May 11, 2007

<Author>JChua
<Content>Nice rooms/views but hotel lacked atmosphere. My mum and I spent two nights, 28-30 April at this wonderful Hotel. Chose this Hotel based mainly on Tripadvisor's high ratings. We knew we were going to arrive at close to midnight from Venice, by Air France coach, hence the obvious choice was to choose this Hotel since we simply cross the road and the Hotel is located right at the corner of Ave Carnot. We were rather happy with our request for a corner room, which offers us 3 balconies with superb views of the Arc de Triomphe. Room was large even by European standards, bed was really really comfortable and the bathroom was simply long and huge! The view at night of the Arc was especially memorable .....Location wise, it is very close to the Metro/RER and shopping in Champs Elysees. Even the Lido Cabaret show was very nearby. However, beware of the underground tunnel closing after 10pm or 11pm. When we were walking back to the Hotel after the Lido show, at around 11.15pm. We had to back tracked and walk above grounds instead. I was a little annoyed cos I emailed the Hotel before my trip and was told to walk back to the Hotel via the underground tunnel? As for breakfasts, managed to catch a glimpse of what's on offer - in my honest opinion, doesn't seem to be worth 22 euros. Right across the Street, you can find nice Cafes which offer breakfast sets at 7.50 or 8.50 euros per person. Finally, I did not grant this wonderful Hotel a full 5 stars rating cos of the lack of atmosphere in the common areas. I thought they should invest some money in decorating the reception and common areas so as to create a cosy/romantic Parisian ambience, which is why millions are visiting Paris each year. After two nights here, we stayed another two nights at the Paris Le-Grand near the Paris Opera, which is by far the most beautiful Parisian hotel I had stayed at (see my review under Paris Le-Grand).  
<Date>May 6, 2007

<Author>Clare_Charnley
<Content>Can't wait to return I found this hotel on tripadvisor.com and booked a superior suite on the hotel's Web site. This trip was a first-time stay in Paris for both my husband and me, and I felt a bit risky doing it all online. However, not only were we awarded the most amazing view I've ever had from a hotel room (the same one w/the view of the Arc on all of their collateral), but we left absolutely singing the praises of the entire staff of the hotel. The pictures we took from one of our threebalconies are the first pictures I show anybody who asks about our trip to Paris. The staff was extremely friendly, courteous, and patient. The location is great and very central. There is a metro stop right across the street as well. The rooms are fine space-wise, especially for Eurpean standards. The bathroom was large and had it's own balcony. And, of course, the room was very clean. My husband and I are in our early thirties, and enjoy good food and wine, both of which were easy to access from the hotel. Not only can I not wait to return to this gem of a hotel, but I am recommending it to anybody who visits Paris.

<Author>amorphous
<Content>All One Could Ask For Having never been to Paris, and having heard many more horror storiesthan positive experiences, I was terrified about selecting a hotel. The Splendid Etoile exceeded every expectation I had. Staff was friendly, courteous, knowledgable, and very helpful. They were excellent English speakers, and put up with our poor attempts at speaking French. The Air France airport bus stops, literally, across the street. Stations for both Metro and RER are right outside the front door. Beyond all that, the view out our window was of the Arc de Tiomphe. Lots of great restaurants and small markets are within just a couple of blocks. All of this combined to make the stay a spectacular one. I was traveling with a spouse, a sister-in-law, and a 16-year-old daughter, and had absolutely no concerns about safety or security inside or outside the hotel. Most interesting, although not most relevant, was that the shower was far better than just aboutany I have experienced in hotels in the US or other European destinations. Plenty of room, good water flow. Beds were comfortable, windows opened, room was as large as it needed to be. I simply couldn't ask for more.

<Content>Fabulous hotel My wife and I stayed at the Splendid Etoile last week to celebrate our 10th wedding anniversary. We chose it because of the excellent reviews on this website. We contacted the hotel direct and requested a superior room with a view of the Arc de Triomphe. The room was lovely and spacious by Parisian standards and WOW....what a view!! We had an uninterrupted view of the Arc and could also see the top half of the Eiffel Tower as it twinkled at night. Very romantic sitting on the balcony, sipping bubbly, looking at these wonderful landmarks.Farooq gets a lot of good press on previous reviews, and rightly so. He makes you feel very welcome. However, without exception, all staff were very courteous, friendly and helpful.The location is fantastic with easy transport access from the airport and a metro station right outside.There's also a fabulous little boulangerie/pattiserie at the bottom of the street with cakes and pastries to die for!.This hotel has everything you could want for a short break in Paris. Without a doubt, when we go back, we'll stay at the Splendid Etoile.

<Author>mamasad
<Content>Splendid Etoile Hotel lives up to its name! We have just returned back from 4 days in Paris, with myself and two children. This hotel totally lives up to its name. Well located by the Arc de Triomphe with a number of rooms that have an excellent view of the Arc. We travelled by metro to the hotel from the Gard du Nord (did Eurostar from London) and the hotel is located immediately in front of an elevator so easy access with luggage on wheels and easy access to the rest of Paris. We stayed in a triple room which was perfect. Our room was large with a seperate area to store our suitcases and plenty of space for clothing. The bathroom was 'awesome' (in the words of my 12 year old daugher!). With very powerful shower and very clean. It faced the front of the hotel on the 6th floor and I was amazed how quiet it was, even though it is on a relatively busy road. My friend also had a triple room at the back of the hotel. This room was even bigger and the bathroom configuration was a little different and equally as good. Cleanliness is a common theme throughout this hotel and the maid service is very impressive and should be commended.You will notice other comments about Farooq, the head of the concierge. This gentleman certainly contributed to the success of our stay. Giving us pertinent information that helped us save money and guided us to the best places to eat and see. The other staff were also incredibly helpful. No question or request appeared too much and we were always greeted with a smile.I have to admit we were nervous about using this hotel given we booked it totally based on tripadvisor.com's recommendation. But we needn't have been worried, we will return for sure.

<Author>patdad
<Content>Great place We stayed at the Splendid Etoile for our friend's 50th birthday celebrations on 11th March. I chose it based on the reviews here and I can assure you that you can believe all the positive comments you read about it. We booked direct and paid 250 euros a room. They are traditionally furnished and well appointed, but to be honest, we hardly spent any time in them, so good was the weather. Room 307 has a perfect view of the Arc de Triomphe; it was a delight to see our friend's face when she saw it! Farooq was charming and very efficient and, yes, he did walk us round the corner to a brasserie he recommended. Use the Air France bus for CDG- at 20 euros return it can't be bettered for price and convenience. Didn't eat breakfast in the hotel - too many cafes around such as the Beer Station where we could sit outside in gloriously sunny weather. We ate well for a very reasonable price at L'amazonial restaurant near Chatelet metro and had a fabulous night out at the Moulin Rouge -it's not cheap, but it's a knockout show you really shouldn't miss. Farooq will book it for you, but as someone else pointed out, he does charge a fee, which wasn't made clear at the time. I would certainly stay there again.

<Author>Datedog
<Content>Fantastic Paris Hotel After much research on this site and others I booked the Hotel Splendid Etoile and it turned out to be a perfect place for our anniversary trip. The location is just amazing. We had a room on the fifth floor (#508) that had not one, but two balconies that overlooked a charming Paris street and had direct views of the Arc de Triomphe and the top half of the Eiffel Tower. To stand out there at night and see the lights while the city rushes by below was just an amazing experience. The service was fantastic. The concerierge, Farooq, was excellent and very knowledgeable about restuarants, transportation and tickets. The hotel was immaculately clean and our room was serviced by the maid twice a day. The bed was comfortable (this room also had a second couch that transistioned into a twin bed in the second sitting room which we didn't need but would be nice for a family). The bathroom was very clean and the water pressure was great. It had a European shower head that could be used in the tub or put on the wall mount that adjusted for your height. The windows were french style doors that were double sets- you actually had to open both sets to get out on the balcony. This design blocks the street noise when the windows are shut. The location just can not be beat. There are restuarants and shopping all around and the metro stop is literally right out the front door (there is an eleveator at street level that takes you directly down to the Charles DeGalle Etoile stop that is a major hub for many metro lines). We could also walk in the under Arc tunnel and be on the Champs Elysees in minutes. Another major bonus was having the Air France bus stop just across the street. (Farooq sold us tickets and we walked out and caught the bus in 10 minutes.) We booked the hotel through Travelocity and got a great deal (which was about $30 less per night than their website or any other site). Overall we were extremely happy with the choice and we would not hesitate to recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>hnewburn
<Content>Not a better choice in Paris After a semi-disastrous stay out in La Defense, my wife and I moved to the Splendid Etoile based on reviews here. We couldn't have made a better choice.A couple of things to be aware of... Like most European rooms, the bed is two twins pushed together and they are a bit low, but not uncomfortable. The pillows were a bit flat, so we got a couple of more, and the AC doesn't work, but they brought us a fan.Having said that, we were in room 505, the top floor that has balconies (there is a 6th floor). Our balcony gave us a wonderful view and the white noise of the traffic and night breezes made for great sleeping. (closing the two double-doors eliminated all but the loudest noises)You can step out the front door to an elevator to the metro/RER station (Charles de Gaulle Etoile). An RER train and two metro lines go through here, making it extremely convenient.Less than 50 meters away is a convenience store to get water, sodas, fruit or snacks that made it highly convenient.The service is just superb. The staff is incredibly gracious and accommodating. When we asked about the AC, they explained it didn't work and there was a fan in our room when we came back. The concierge, bellman and desk people are all wonderful.The room itself is spacious, a nice size bathroom, a tub/shower with an adjustable spray head that can be hand held, incredible water pressure and scalding heat if needed. The closet is spacious and there's plenty of room for your luggage. A flat screen TV with three news channels in English, they don't have in-room movies, but we didn't miss them.There is in-room wired internet for 14 euros / day. There's also an Orange France hot-spot with a 98% signal that you can use with subscriber plans like T-Mobile.For price, location and convenience I just can't see how it can get better than this.

<Author>DevaEboracum
<Content>A Great Hotel With Great Service Everything written here in previous reviews about how good this hotel is are totally accurate.The hotel is in a perfect location - 1 minute from the Arc D'triumph. In fact, from our room (406) you could open the window, walk onto the balcony, and there it was to the right. The cleaners started banging around in the cupboard at about 8.00am and because it was right next to a hollow, fully tiled bathroom, the sound was quite loud. So my only quibble is - if you want to have an undisturbed late lie in bed, room 406 is not the room to have.

<Content>Great hotel at this price. Had a 5 day, 4 night stay at the Splendid Etoile Hotel in Paris at the end of November 2006. Our room had a sideway view of the Arc which was 鈥渟plendid鈥? Perhaps a 20-30 minute walk to many of the good tourist sites. The breakfast was chargeable at about 15 Euros per person, so we didn鈥檛 avail ourselves of that, preferring the local restaurants. Two sets of huge glass doors kept out all street noise but we left them open during the day just to listen to Paris! <Content>Charming Hotel, Pleasant Service, Excellent Location! My husband and I just returned from an incredible trip to Paris. It was our first time visiting the romantic city and we had an unforgettable time. For three nights we stayed in a Superior Room at the Splendid Etoile hotel. We enjoyed everything about it. Our room/bathroom was large and comfortable, the elegant d茅cor was warm and inviting, and the view of the Arc de Triumph from our balcony was amazing! We found the staff and concierge were pleasant and helpful. One morning we asked the concierge for restaurant recommendations for dinner and he happily made us reservations at a wonderful French restaurant down the street called 鈥淟e Petit Colombier.鈥?The fixed price menu had great choices and the overall dining experience was excellent. Another appealing feature of the hotel is the convenient location and access to public transportation. There are many taxi stands, RER and Metro locations surrounding the hotel. (We purchased a 3-day Paris Visite pass which granted unlimited travel in Paris using the RER, Metro, and bus systems. This was a great hassle-free way to travel the city.) Also, the Air France Shuttle (20 Euros/person round trip) is relaxing way to get to and from the airport. The shuttle leaves Charles de Gaulle airport and travels to two locations in downtown Paris. One of the drop off/ pick-up points is right across the street from the Splendid Etoile.We recommend this hotel to others looking for a Parisian hotel with charm and elegance. We would definitely stay at this hotel again on our next trip to Paris.

L'Arc, the Eiffel Tower lit up. Oh yes, the bathroom was great - large with a bath and shower.We wanted somewhere within walking distance for our Saturday night out and got some recommendations from the girls in the MAC makeup shop (always a winner). We found such a cool bar down Rue de Berri (on the left as you walk down the Champs Elysee from the hotel). Its called QUEENIE. Very STC, great cocktails. Then we went onto a bar/club called Le Sens. Seriously cool! Lovely decor. Expensive drinks but it was very nice in there! We were there at midnight however and it was pretty empty... apparently it fills up around 2am. So we left and went to another club called Blanche just around the corner. It was packed (younger age group... Im 33, my friend is 20) but really good, everyone dancing and having a good time. We stayed in there until 5am....!Anyway just adding these tips about bars and clubs as I always appreciate recommendations in foreign cities so I know Im gonna have a great night out :-)I thoroughly recommend this hotel. It was really good all round and just opposite is a great cafe/restaurant for breakfast or lunch. We had breakfast there and the waiter gave my friend his number - what more do you want in Paris?!?

<Author>Marais1969
<Content>Great Location, Staff and Room This hotel is located across the street from the AirFrance bus stop so, for 13 Euros, you can have a very easy trip from CDG airport to your hotel. There is a metro stop directly outside the hotel room door and the station is serviced by the 1, 2 and 6 metro lines (along with an RER train, I believe). This makes it convenient to travel to many locations without switching trains (including the Louvre and Place De La Bastille).If you want a drink after a day roaming paris, L'Ecluse wine bar is just down the street. Breakfast may be purchased at one of the many cafe's within 1 block of the hotel, or at the patisserie/boulangerie also located in close proximity to the hotel.Paolo, Farooq and the rest of the staff were outstanding, helpful hosts.I booked a superior room for 10 days. The room and bathroom were clean, bright and comfortable. Cleaning staff was excellent. The hotel was quiet.

<Author>QueenMimi
<Content>Great location in Paris We got off the Air France plane, walked on to the Air France bus that dropped us off across the street from this hotel. You can't get easier than that. We took one to Bercy station and it cost 20Euros. All the people that were working at the hotel, especially Farooq, were helpful and courteous.

<Author>Bernlh
<Content>Lovely Paris My partner and I visited Paris for three days in April this year and apart from the fact that it was a little cold - it was wonderful. Upon arriving at Charles DeGuille we were a little confused with travelling into Paris, however, in the end decided on taking the train. This hotel is on a train line and the public transport train system in Paris is amazing - once we were on the train, we had no trouble finding it. We were upgraded to I would have to say the best room in the hotel, which had french windows that opened up to a view of the Eifel Tower - we were both speechless for about 10 minutes. The view at night was breathtaking - the Eifel Tower has sparkling lights every hour on the hour - again amazing. The room wasn't too big, but it served it's purpose for us, it was neat and clean - on our first night we found a little grocery store and bought wine, cheese, bread and meat and set up the couch in front of the french windows and watched the Eifel Tower. If ever we have the chance to visit Paris again we will definately stay there again. It is close to everything, or within distance of a bus or train very easy to get around. Highly recommend.

<Author>travelermia
<Content>C'est Magnifique! Just returned from a week at the Splendid Etoile on our very first trip to Paris. Kudos to the hotel and its staff for operating such a well-run property. Superlatives include: Farooq and other front desk staff who were friendly, knowledgeable, and went out of their way to book excursions for us and show us exactly which Metro lines to take; spacious room; comfortable queen size bed (we had the superior room); air conditioning controls in the room; hot breakfast (15 euros); location as has been mentioned previously; close to great shopping- Louis Vuitton store (be prepared to stand in line to get in) and Hugo Boss and of course fabulous restaurants just a few blocks down on the marvelous Champs-Elysee. The only thing we did not like about the hotel were the towels. We're used to plush towels both at home and away; theirs were very thin and we felt we could never be dry enough. Oh well, one small ripple in a sea of superlatives. Paris is lovely and the people absolutely delightful. I do not know why Parisians have gotten such a bad rap from Americans. Maybe its from people who have never traveled there. They are polite and respectul people who went out of their way to help us; total strangers on the metro and on the street offered to help us find our way when they saw fumbling with our maps. I speak a little French, but most people wanted to speak English to us. We went to every neighborhood and tourist attraction you can imagine so we got a pretty good taste of the entire city. We always felt safe; no one at all bothered us. If you must see anything in Paris, don't miss the Louvre (Sundays it's free admission, as it's on Wednesdays after 3:00 p.m and the lines are short); Musee Orsay; Saint Chapelle; the ride up to the top of the Eiffel Tower; and if you have time, Versailles and Giverny (Claude Monet's home) which the hotel can arrange for about 143 euros per person for an 8 hour trip). All around this was the best vacation we've ever taken. We're already planning our next vacation to Paris, quite simply the most wonderful city in the world. We would consider the Spledid Etoile for our next stay, but we would probably stay some where else just to try a new hotel.Bon voyage!  
<Date>Oct 6, 2006

<Author>jrzjenn
<Content>Very Nice, would recommend Stayed at the hotel for 8 days in September 2006 with my boyfriend, we're 29  36. Found it to be exactly as others describle. I thought the room was great, rm 403. Big bathroom, lots of closet/drawer space, excellent a/c and 2 french doors to the balcony with view of Arc. The hotel never seemed crowded, the staff was helpful and spoke excellent English. I like that you never had to carry your key around they hold it at the front desk. We did return every night after the doors were locked and never waited more than a few minutes for them to open it for us.The hotel was very centralized, the Metro across the street is on the popular line that goes down the Champs Elysees -Louvre, very convenient. We also went to Versailles ourselves and it was about an hour total between taking 2 trains. Taxi stand was right in front of the hotel and it was never hard to get a taxi. Also we got the AirFrance shuttle navette (it's more like a bus) to and from the airport, 12E each way. Slightly confusing taking to the hotel, very easy taking it back. Make sure you have the hotel confirm your terminal before leaving since we got off on the wrong one and had to take another bus to the right one!We ate at the cafe La Flame around the corner for dinner/drinks on 2 occaisons, reasonable prices, great atmosphere. We also ate a fast breakfast one morning at the Quick fast food place 2 blocks away. We also at a few places along the Champs, Madigral and L'Alsace.... service was ok, food was mediocre, very pricey. Laduree was excellent!! We loved Barrio Latino in the Bastile area, great food and great music, dance floor was packed and fun to watch. We also liked the food court in the Lourve for a quick lunch. Le Petit Pont was a nice place to eat right across from Notre Dame, we also liked the live jazz at Le Caveau de la Hauchette. Lots of bars/cafes/nightlife on that street.We saw the Lido show and the Crazy Horse cabaret, Farooq the concierge, booked our tickets, he charged us 32E as a fee, the seats were great and we did get free champagne at the Lido, but just be aware he has a booking fee. Both shows were great I would recommend both. We did the entire city in 8 days, there is so much to see, we walked a million miles and the weather was hot for September, 85F. Always took a nap before heading out around 9pm for dinner. It was a great trip, I did a lot of research on the hotel and was glad that the Spendid Etoile was exactly what we expected!

<Author>BrookeBD
<Content>Highly recommend this hotel I was very nervous booking a hotel on Travelocity since I had never been to Paris. It turned out the be better that we could have expected. We were in Paris for 4 days and loved it. I think our impression of the entire city had a lot to do with the hotel. Fantastic location - we walked everywhere, but it wasn't loud or crowded right outside the hotel. Great view - we had a corner room with a direct view of the Arc de Triomphe, just like the pictures on the internet show. The room was spacious, especially the bathroom. The staff at the front desk made us feel so welcome. They were friendly, happy to speak English, and gave great suggestions for restaurants and photo opportunities. They also kept our luggage after we checked out the last day so we could spend a few more hours enjoying the city. A few tips - take the Air France bus to and from the hotel if you are flying into the city. It was so easy, just as quick as a taxi, and it stops in front of the hotel. You can even buy tickets at the front desk. Buy some bottled water and snacks at the grocery store (we found one a block or so from the hotel). It is hard to find a cheap bite to eat when you are out touring the city.

<Author>leeamm
<Content>Perfect Paris Getaway! If you are looking for a hotel with a real Parisian feel, look no further! We booked the Splendid Etoile by the positive reviews on Trip Advisor months ago for our 30th wedding anniversary getaway and it ended up being exactly what we wanted. Our room was #207 and it was perfect. Having a corner room wrap around balcony, with three floor to ceiling french doors - one in the bath and two in the bedroom/sitting area. French furnishings, a crystal chandelier and a large marble bathroom. A flat screen tv too! not that you will be watching much tv but a daily news report in English was nice to keep in touch with the world even while on vacation.This was our first trip to Paris and we wanted a hotel that was quaint, French, accommodating, clean, convenient to the Metro/transportation and near the Champs Elysees for evening walks. The Splendid fit all of our needs. The location was a few blocks from the Champs but was surprisingly quiet even with the french doors opened. The location is near many restaurants, cafes, bars, bakeries, wine shops, etc. Also the CDG/Air France bus stops on the opposite corner so getting to and from the airport is a breeze and less expensive than taking a cab. Buy the round trip ticket for the bus for a good deal. The Metro stop was right outside the door of the hotel and we used only the Metro for getting around the city. We also booked a couple of excursions thru a travel company that picked us up by minivan at the door of the Splendid Etoile as well. Walking to the Champs Elysees a few evenings for dinner and people watching was very nice and a lovely stroll among the neighborhood getting there.The staff--especially Farooq-- was the best. Always greeted us and spoke perfect English, thank goodness, since our French consisted of only a few words and phrases. Farooq was very knowledgable and more than accommodating about any questions we had, going over and above aiding us with helpful hints, good suggestions and general French info. He is by far the best concierge we have ever used! The rest of the staff were also very pleasant and helpful. The room we booked was a superior and very spacious, clean, with a french style decor-- silk wall coverings, draperies, furnishings, and the balcony with a wonderful view of the Arc d' Triomphe!!!! We never had breakfast or dinner at the hotel so we can not comment on the dining experience at the hotel. But right across the street is a nice restaurant  L'Emporieur that had a delicious menu. We never had a bad meal there.........ate a few breakfasts and dinners there. Authentic french fare........duck, chicken with mustard sauce, jambon and fromage sandwiches, omelets, chocolate crescents........And the best steak, potatoes and dessert we had in the city all week was at this little cafe! And that is saying a lot since we didnt have a bad meal all week no matter where we happened to eat.....from the bakeries, street fare, bistros or expensive restaurants......... So you dont have to walk all over the city looking for a good place to dine every night when L'Emporieur is so close by. And the staff there are very nice too! We highly recommend this hotel!!!!

<Author>Anita63
<Content>Great Place! There are plenty of reviews of this hotel, all mostly raving about it. This review is positive, but not over the top as I've been told that I am rather picky about where I stay (ahem!).1. Price: There is no such thing as a bargain in Paris and you will get what you pay for. To find this hotel in a good area, clean, helpful staff, great views, around the $250 CAD price point was acceptable. 2. Cleanliness:It is clean, but it is not spotless, it is an old hotel, but it certainly did not creep me out. The fact that I didn't leave is testimony that the place was acceptable (I have left more hotels upon arrival than I care to mention).3. Room: Bigger than I thought it would have been!! Rooms are SMALL in Paris and this room was on the large size (407). I had three balconies...two with views of the Arc and one balcony off the bathroom which was different. King size bed with a seperate door was nice. Furnishings were nice, nothing fancy, but not a la 'Days Inn' either. Closet and safe. Bathroom is a weird configuration. Watch your step out of shower as it is higher/deeper to step to floor than in North America.4. Location: Very close to shopping,food, metro,and taxi's. Area is more congested than I like, but it's Paris and crowds are part of the deal. Metro is best bet for getting around and Air France bus is best bet for getting to and from airport (CDG).5. Staff: Faraque (sp?) was everything and more that people have already written. Very pleasant, accomodating, knowledgable. Unfortunately he only worked one day of the four I was there and I had to deal with the less experienced staff. Two things that left me puzzled with his staff: I purchased 6 stamps from the front desk at .90E each and I was charged 9.0E in total. That is either a hell of a service charge or the staff can't add. And secondly, DO NOT ASK THEM TO GET A CAB FOR YOU. There are usually plenty of cabs just outside the hotel to the right that start the meter at 0, but when the staff called me a cab (I didn't notice the other ones outside, like an idiot) the cab arrived from several blocks away and there was already 6 Euro's on the meter. I meant to take that up with the hotel, but ran out of time. Rediculous to pay $10 more for a cab ride b/c they called.6. Food: Did not eat at hotel at all, so I cannot comment. Lots of choices locally and everything was good albeit expensive (but again, that is Paris for you).7. Elevator: Small is an understatement, but it is good for a laugh and photo. The staircase was very nice and very typical Parisian.8. Overall Comments: Nice place to stay, a bit far from the Seine, satisfactory experience. Not luxury by any stretch of the imagination (especially after visiting the Hemingway Bar at the Ritz one night...now THAT is luxury), but more like a really nice Best Western.

<Author>Kenya2010
<Content>So sorry, but can't recommend to friends and family We spent a week at the Hotel Splendid Etoile in the late July. We chose this hotel based upon its fabulous location, and the positive TA reviews. Reservations were made on line, with hotel staff, who were very acommodating and pleasant via email. Our request for a room with a view of the Arc was granted, and we were given a lovely corner room with an updated marble bathroom. The hotel is rather plain and charmless, but the rooms are well-soundproofed and pretty, the location is fantastic and we were quite comfortable throughout our stay. Sadly, I cannot recommend the hotel, though. The front desk staff are not uniformly pleasant and helpful. I speak some high school/college french, and they all speak excellent english, so it was certainly not a language issue.We would have been happy to recommend the hotel, were it not for one extremely unpleasant incident. The airconditioning system in our room was not functioning properly, and we were startled to find one afternoon, a sopping wet rug beneath the ceiling unit -- apparently from dripping condensation. The moisture was so great that the unit also dripped water in to the adjacent closet where my husbands clothes were stacked on the shelf. His clothes were soaked. A poorly functioning airconditioner is certainly not reason to be unhappy with the hotel, but what happened next is. My husband took his wet clothes down to the front desk to explain the situation. He requested that the clothes be cleaned, and that someone come look at the unit. A very nice young man saw the soaked carpet, and sent a repairman shortly thereafter. As it was a Sunday, the repairman was not a professional, and did nothing to repair the unit. The next Monday, while breakfasting downstairs, the day manager approached us at our table. She told us that according to the repairman, there was nothing wrong with the airconditioning unit, and that if we wanted our clothes cleaned, we would have to pay for it. My husband and I were flabbergasted. We are very honest people, and would never THINK of creating such an elaborate scam to get clothes cleaned. I took the manager up to our room, where she saw the wet rug and visible water drips on the wall. This was her opportunity to offer up a heartfelt apology, but it never came. She insisted that it was reasonable policy to assume the worst of the guests (after all, just that morning, some guests had run off with 80 euros of mini-bar). She explained to me that, You would be surprised at the things people will do to get their laundry done.I found this behavior unprofessional and simply, unkind. Call me naive, but I thought people went in to the hospitality business because they genuinely like serving the public. This particular manager seemed not to like her job, let alone people.Although I can't recommend the hotel for the above reason, it has its strong points. If you do stay there, don't expect pleasant, professional treatment from all the front desk staff.  
<Date>Aug 6, 2006

<Author>Rachael_David
<Content>Fantastic Location My husband and I have just returned from a four night trip to the Splendid Etoile Hotel.The first good point about this hotel is that the Air France bus from CDG Airport stops just over the road from the hotel which eliminates the stress of trying to find your hotel!Secondly, the room we recieved had the most amazing view of the Arc de Triomphe and the Eiffel Tower. We paid for a Superior room and as it was our 1st Wedding Anniversary I requested a nice view, the reservations lady, Francoise, was so helpful and she gave us the best room she had. All of the staff at the hotel are lovely and speak really good english.Thirdly, it is so easy to get back to the hotel after walking around Paris as all you have to do is find the Arc de Triomphe!! And that is really not hard at all!The only thing we were dissapointed about in Paris was the Eiffel Tower, obviously the view from the top is fantastic but we waited around two hours to actually get a ticket and get to the second floor and then again we waited another 1/2 hour to get to the top. The queing system is non existant and it is pretty much a stampede to get into a lift. Not a nice experience however we can say that we have been to the top of the Eiffel Tower!!!I hope this short review has helped others in deciding that the Spelndid Etoile is for them, do not hesitate to book this hotel.Rachael  David x

<Author>JPC4
<Content>Super hotel The Hotel Splendid de Etoile located on Avenue Carnot is a fine hotel and I recommend it. My family, wife and two teenage girls, are very picky when it comes to cleanliness and comfort. The Splendid ranked pretty high in their book. Nicely decorated, it is a bit Spartan, but again, for us,clean and comfortable. The bathrooms are large and function well. They could use some new tile and updating, but otherwise fine. The rooms were larger than I expected and larger than the ones we found in London. The furniture which could use some updating is just fine and fits the hotel well. What makes this hotel a killer place to stay however is the view of the Arch de Triumph. As requested when making the internet reservations, we received a corner room on the 4th floor and an adjacent one on Avenue Carnot. My wife and I took the corner with two balconies. We spent each evening parked in our chairs on the balcony with a glass of wine in full view of the Arch. The girls had a room with one balcony which had a partial (can see most) view. Fantastic! There are some suites with better views, but there are some rooms I am certain with no views, so, make the effort to request these if you are interested.The hotel staff is helpful yet unobtrusive. We did not eat in the hotel at all. For water, snacks, wine and even fruit, we walked about less than a block to a small market on a side street. For breakfast there is a nice caf茅 across the street. We had a great pasta meal at another caf茅 within eyesight of our balcony on the next block. The metro stop, as most have pointed out, is accessible by elevator just outside the front door of the hotel, or by stairs across the street. Note: my wife almost had her wallet lifted from her purse on the Paris Metro (not hotel related), but because she has a habit of keeping her hand over the front top 鈥搊pening purse, she actually caught the girl鈥檚 hand as it was trying to lift the contents. There were two of them in their late teens and they jostled her away from the hand grip as she boarded and used the distraction for one to try the lift. Be careful.

<Author>Cfarley
<Content>Splendid is Splendid! My wife and I stayed at the Splendid Etoile for 5 days in early April. You can't beat the location. We could see the Arc De Triomphe(spelling) from our window! You have an elevator to the Metro right outside the Hotel doors. Don't take a cab from the Airport, there's an Air France shuttle that takes you right to the hotel. Get a round trip ticket, it's cheaper than 2 one ways. Didn't eat in Hotel, too expensive. There's a great cafe down the street where you can get coffee and pastries on the cheap. Nice staff but try to speak a little French or they can be a little snotty, but then again you're in France! Enjoy!

<Author>Mainers
<Content>Wonderful Hotel! We too were a little concerned when we saw the TA rating drop from #3 to #18, but NOT to worry, this place is a gem! We had a standard triple room, with 3 single beds (traveling w our daughter). The room was on the 2nd floor so I was concerned about noise -- but even on lower floors this hotel is wonderfully quiet, not only do the double french doors block out virtually all traffice noise, but a/c and plumbing were very quiet. We were amazed at how quiet it was. The room had a view of the Arc from the balcony, was quite spacious (for a hotel in the heart of the city), high ceilings which gave it an open feel, lovely French furnishings, and a bathroom that was quite large, including two sinks (a real plus with a teenager). It also had a very nice feature - you could close off the entry area to have privacy when getting dressed or using bathroom. As reported, metro is right at your doorstep and Farooq is great at directing you to the sights. He not only told us about which metro to take, but also the exact number of stops between the hotel and the destination! The room was ready early (about 11am), so we were able to clean up after the long flight, before leaving to sightsee. We found all the staff at the front desk to be very helpful, pleasant and professional. Farooq was on vacation for a couple of days, and his replacemt was reallly very nice. We would stay here again and recommend it to others without reservation, esp the triple room.

We had a balcony with views of the Arc de Triomphe and the top portion of the Eiffel Tower. The metro stop is right across the street and the Champs-Elysees is within sight of the hotel. The housekeeping staff had our room cleaned within a few minutes of our departure each day. Robes and even washcloths are provided!! Room service delivered coffee each morning for only 10 Euro for two, which is less than many of the local cafes. The front desk staff were helpful and accommodating. We booked directly through the hotel website so breakfast was not included in the price of our room. At 16 Euro for Continental or 23 Euro for full breakfast, it was pricey, but the many cafes nearby offer better value. We would highly recommend the Splendid Etoile!
